25:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part. Be mindful of God, and He will teach you: He has full knowledge of everything26:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part.                   <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, originally <foreign lang="ar">وَحَدٌ</foreign>, the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> being changed into <foreign lang="ar">أ</foreign>, (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">One;</hi> the <hi rend="ital">first of the numbers;</hi> (S;) syn. [in many cases] with <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign>; (S, Msb, K;) with which it is interchangeable in two cases, to be explained below: (Msb:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">آحَادٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أٌحْدَانٌ</foreign> (K) and <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدُونَ</foreign>, which last occurs in a phrase hereafter to be mentioned; (TA;) or it has no pl. in this sense; (Msb, K, * TA;) and as to <foreign lang="ar">آحَادٌ</foreign>, it may be pl. of <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign>, [and originally <foreign lang="ar">أَوْحَادٌ</foreign>,] like <foreign lang="ar">أَشْهَادٌ</foreign> as pl. of <foreign lang="ar">شَاهِدٌ</foreign>, (Th, Msb,) a pl. of pauc. (Msb.) The fem. is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n333-1" target="إِحْدَى" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n7401"/></foreign> only; and this is only used in particular cases, to be shown below: (Msb:) most agree that the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> in this word is the characteristic of the fem. gender: but some say that it is to render it quasi-coordinate to the quadriliteral-radical class: [this, however, is inconsistent with its pronunciation, which is invariably <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى</foreign>, not <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَّى</foreign>:] (TA:) its pl. is <foreign lang="ar">إِحَدٌ</foreign>, as though the sing. were <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَةٌ</foreign>, like as is said of <foreign lang="ar">ذِكَرٌ</foreign> as pl. of <foreign lang="ar">ذِكْرَى</foreign>: one of the expositors of the Tes-heel writes it <foreign lang="ar">أُحَدٌ</foreign>, with damm and then fet-h; but a pl. of this measure is not applicable to a sing. of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فِعْلَى</foreign>, with kesr. (MF.) The dim. of <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign> is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n333-2" target="أُحَيْدٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n338"/></foreign>; and that of <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى</foreign> is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n333-3" target="أُحَيْدَى" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n340"/></foreign>. (L in art. <foreign lang="ar">وحد</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  It is interchangeable with <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign> in two cases: first, when it is used as an epithet applied to God: (Msb:) for <foreign lang="ar">الأَحَدُ</foreign>, as an epithet, is applied to God alone, (Msb, K,) and signifies <hi rend="ital">The One; the Sole; He who has ever been one and alone:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the Indivisible:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">He who has no second</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to share</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in his lordship, nor in his essence, nor in his attributes:</hi> (TA:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ الوَاحِدُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ الأَحَدُ</foreign>: and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign>, without the article, is used as an epithet specially in relation to God, and is interchangeable in this case [but not in other cases] with <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign>: therefore you do not say <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ أَحَدٌ</foreign> nor <foreign lang="ar">دِرْهَمٌ أَحَدٌ</foreign> and the like [but <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَاحدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">دِرهَمٌ وَاحِدٌ</foreign> &amp;c.] (Msb.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign>, in art. <foreign lang="ar">وحد</foreign>.] In the phrase in the Kur [cxii. 1], <foreign lang="ar">قُلْ هُوَ اللّٰهُ أَحَدٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Say, He is God, One</hi> God], <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign> is a substitute for <foreign lang="ar">اللّٰهُ</foreign>; for an indeterminate noun is sometimes a substitute for a determinate noun, as in another passage in the Kur, xcvi. 15 and 16. (S.) Secondly, it is interchangeable with <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign> in certain nouns of number: (Msb:) you say <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدَ عَشَرَ</foreign> [masc.] and <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى عَشْرَةَ</foreign> [fem.] (S) [meaning <hi rend="ital">Eleven:</hi> and in these two cases you may not substitute <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدَةٌ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى</foreign>: but] in <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌوعَشْرُونَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">One and twenty,</hi> and the like,] <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign> is interchangeable with <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign>. (Msb.) Ks says, When you prefix the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign> to a number, prefix it to every number; therefore you should say, <foreign lang="ar">مَا فَعَلَتِ الأَحَدَ العَشَرَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَلْفَ الدِّرْهَمَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">What did the eleven thousand dirhems?</hi>]: but the Basrees prefix it to the first only, and say, <foreign lang="ar">ما فعلت الأَحَدَ عَشَرَ أَلْفَ دِرْهَمٍ</foreign>. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  In [most] cases differing from these two, there is a difference in usage between <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign>: the former is used in affirmative phrases as a prefixed noun only, governing the noun which follows it in the gen. case; [as in exs. which will be found below;] and is used absolutely in negative phrases; [as will also be seen in exs. below;] whereas <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign> is used in affirmative phrases as a prefixed noun and otherwise: the fem. <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى</foreign>, also, is only used as a prefixed noun, except in numbers (Msb) [and in one other instance, which see below]. Using <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign> and its fem. in affirmative phrases as prefixed nouns, you say, <foreign lang="ar">قَامَ أَحَدُ الثَّلَاثَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">One of the three stood</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">قَالَتْ إِحْدَا هُمَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">One of them two</hi> (females) <hi rend="ital">said</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">خُذْ إِحْدَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الثَّلَاثَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Take thou one of the three</hi>]. (TA.) The phrase <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى بَنَاتِ طَبَقٍ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">A calamity:</hi> (K:) or, as some say, (TA, but in the K “ and, ”) <hi rend="ital">a serpent;</hi> (K, TA;) so called because it twists itself round so as to become like a <foreign lang="ar">طَبَق</foreign>. (TA.) And the phrase <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى الإِحَدِ</foreign>, (L, K, TA,) in which the latter word has kesr to the <foreign lang="ar">إ</foreign> and fet-h to the <foreign lang="ar">ح</foreign>, and is pl. of the former, also written <foreign lang="ar">الأُحَدِ</foreign>, but this form is disapproved by MF, as has been shown above, (TA, [in several copies of the K incorrectly written <foreign lang="ar">الأَحَدِ</foreign>,]) [lit. means <hi rend="ital">One of the ones;</hi> and] is applied to <hi rend="ital">a great,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mighty, event;</hi> (L, K, TA;) <hi rend="ital">one that is difficult, distressing, grievous,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">terrible.</hi> (L, TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">أَتَى بِإِحْدَى الإِحَدِ</foreign> [the last of which words is here again written in several copies of the K <foreign lang="ar">الأَحَدِ</foreign>] <hi rend="ital">He brought to pass a grievous, and great,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mighty, event,</hi> (K, TA,) when you desire to express the greatness and terribleness of an event. (TA.) You also say, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانُ أَحَدُ الأَحَدِينَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدُ الأَحَدِينَ</foreign>, (K, TA,) the latter in one copy of the K written <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدُ الوَاحِدِينَ</foreign>, in which the latter word is pl. of the former, (TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الآحَادِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى الإِحَدِ</foreign>, (K, TA,) like a phrase before mentioned, only the former is applied to a calamity, and this to an intelligent being, and written in the two manners before mentioned, the difference being only in application, (TA, [in several copies of the K here again written <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَحَدِ</foreign>, and in the CK <foreign lang="ar">اَحَدِىُّ الاَحَدِ</foreign>,]) and <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَحَدِينَ</foreign>, (Et-Tes-heel,) and <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى الآحَادِ</foreign>, (TA,) which are expressions of the utmost praise, (IAar, A Heyth, K,) [lit. <hi rend="ital">Such a man is one of the ones;</hi> meaning] <hi rend="ital">such a one is unique among the uniques;</hi> (TA;) <hi rend="ital">one who has no equal; unequalled; incomparable.</hi> (IAar, Tes-heel.) It seems that the form of pl. used in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدُ الأَحَدِينَ</foreign> is used only as applied to rational beings; but it is said in the Expositions of the Tes-heel that this phrase signifies <hi rend="ital">One of the calamities;</hi> the form of the rational pl. being given to nouns significant of things deemed great, mighty, or grievous. (AHeyth.) In the phrase <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى الإِحَدِ</foreign>, the fem. forms are said to be used for the purpose of giving intensiveness to the signification, as though the meaning were <foreign lang="ar">دَاهِيَةُ الدَّوَاهِى</foreign>, the word <foreign lang="ar">داهية</foreign> being [an intensive epithet] from <foreign lang="ar">دَهَآءٌ</foreign> as signifying intelligence, or intelligence mixed with craft or cunning and forecast; or by <foreign lang="ar">داهية</foreign> being meant a calamity. (Expositions of the Fs, TA.) AHei thought <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدُ الأَحَدِينَ</foreign> to be an epithet applied to a male, and <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى الإِحَدِ</foreign> to be applied to a female: but his opinion has been refuted by EdDemámeenee in the Expos. of the Tes-heel: and this latter author there remarks, that in expressions meant to denote praise [of a man], <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى</foreign> are prefixed to their own proper pls., as <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدُونَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">إِحَدٌ</foreign>; or to an epithet, as in the case of <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدُ العُلَمَآءِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">One of the learned</hi>]; but that they have not been heard prefixed to generic nouns. (TA.) You say likewise, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ ٱبْنُ إِحْدَاهَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He is born of noble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">generous, ancestors, both on the father's and the mother's side;</hi> speaking of a man and of a camel. (L and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">وحد</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">لَا يَقُومُ بِهٰذَا الأَمْرِ إِلَّا ٱبْنُ إِحْدَاهَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">None will manage this thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affair, but a noble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">generous, man.</hi> (AZ, L in art. <foreign lang="ar">وحد</foreign>.) And   
      <foreign lang="ar">لَا <ref cref="n333-4" target="يَسْتَطِيعُهَا" n="4" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF"/> ٱبْنُ إِحْداتِهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">None will be able to perform it but a noble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">generous, man</hi>]. (L in art. <foreign lang="ar">وحد</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  One instance is mentioned, of the occurrence, in a trad., of <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى</foreign> not used as a part of a number [i. e. not as a part of the compound <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى عَشْرَةَ</foreign>] nor as a prefixed noun; viz., <foreign lang="ar">إِحْدَى مِنْ سَبْعٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">One of seven</hi>]; in which <foreign lang="ar">سبع</foreign> is said to mean the nights of 'Ád [during which that tribe was destroyed], or the years of Joseph [during which Egypt was afflicted with dearth]. (MF, from the Fáïk &amp;c.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  Used in a negative phrase, <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">Any one with whom one may talk or speak:</hi> and in this manner it is used without variation as sing. and pl. and fem. (S) as well as masc. (Msb.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَحَدَ فِي الدَّارِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">There is not any one in the house</hi>]: but you do not say, <foreign lang="ar">فِيهَا أَحَدٌ</foreign> [as meaning the contrary]. (S.) We read in the Kur [lxix. 47, this ex. of its use as a masc. pl.], <foreign lang="ar">فَمَا مِنْكُمْ مِنْ أَحَدٍ عَنْهُ حَاجِزِينَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And not any persons of you should have withheld me from</hi> punishing <hi rend="ital">him</hi>]. (S.) And in the same [xxxiii. 32, we find this ex. of its use as a fem. pl.], <foreign lang="ar">لَسْتُنَّ كَأَحَدٍ مِنَ النِّسَآءِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Ye are not like any</hi> others <hi rend="ital">of women</hi>]. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  It is also used in interrogative phrases; as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">هَلْ أَحَدٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَأَي مِثْلَ هٰذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Has any one seen the like of this?</hi>]; (A'Obeyd, L;) and in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">يَا حَدْ رَآهَا</foreign> [for <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَحَدٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">O, has any one seen her,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it?</hi>]. (L, from a trad.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  It is [said to be] also used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">شَىءٌ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">Anything</hi>], applied to an irrational being; as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">مَا بِا لدَّارِ مِنْ أَحَدٍ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">إِلَّا حِمَارًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">There is not in the house anything,</hi> rational or irrational, <hi rend="ital">except an ass:</hi> so that the thing excepted is united in kind to that from which the exception is made [accord. to this rendering; but this instance is generally regarded as one in which the thing excepted is disunited in kind from that from which the exception is made]. <pb n="28"/> (Msb.) So too in the Kur lx. 11, accord. to the reading of Ibn-Mes'ood: (Msb:) but others there read <foreign lang="ar">شَىْءٌ</foreign>, which may mean any one or any thing. (Bd, Jel.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الأَحَدٌ</foreign>, (K,) as also <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمَ الأَحَدِ</foreign>, (S, Msb,) as a proper name, (Msb,) is applied to <hi rend="ital">A certain day;</hi> (K;) [<hi rend="ital">Sunday;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the first day of the week;</hi> or, as some say, [i. e. as some term it,] <hi rend="ital">the second of the week;</hi> (TA;) for the Arabs are said, by IAar, to have reckoned the Sabbath, or Saturday, as the first, though they called Sunday the first of the days: (Msb in art. <foreign lang="ar">جمع</foreign>:) it is sing., and masc.: (Lh:) pl. [as above, i. e.] <foreign lang="ar">آحَادٌ</foreign> (S, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">أُحْدَانٌ</foreign>: (K:) or it has no pl. (K: [but in the TA this last observation is very properly restricted, as relating only to <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign> as syn. with <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign>, and as applied to any unknown person.]) In this sense, it has no dim. (Sb, in S, art. <foreign lang="ar">امس</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الآحَادُ</foreign> in lexicology signifies <hi rend="ital">What have been transmitted by some of the lexicologists, but not by such a number of them as cannot be supposed to have agreed to a falsehood:</hi> what has been transmitted by this larger number is termed <foreign lang="ar">مُتَوَاتِرُ</foreign>. (Mz 3rd <foreign lang="ar">نوع</foreign>.)    </entryFree>2a:T5a2,<entryFree id="n337" key="أُحَادَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أُحَادَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [accus. of <foreign lang="ar">أُحَادُ</foreign>] is imperfectly decl., because of its deviation from its original, (S, K,) both in form and in meaning; (S;) [being changed in form from <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدًا</foreign>, and in meaning from <foreign lang="ar">ٱوَاحِدًا</foreign>: (see <foreign lang="ar">ثُلَاثَ</foreign>:)] you say, <foreign lang="ar">جَاؤُوا أُحَادَ أُحَادَ</foreign>, [<foreign lang="ar">احاد</foreign> being repeated for the purpose of corroboration,] meaning, <hi rend="ital">They came one</hi> [<hi rend="ital">and</hi>] <hi rend="ital">one, one</hi> [<hi rend="ital">and</hi>] <hi rend="ital">one;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">one</hi> [<hi rend="ital">by</hi>] <hi rend="ital">one, one</hi> [<hi rend="ital">by</hi>] <hi rend="ital">one.</hi> (S, K.) The dim. of <foreign lang="ar">أُحَادُ</foreign> is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n337-1" target="أُحَيِّدٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n339"/></foreign>, perfectly decl., like <foreign lang="ar">ثُلَيِّثٌ</foreign> [q. v.] &amp;c.
